## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration in such systems typically arises from restoring forces (functions of x) and damping forces (functions of v), possibly with nonlinear terms like cubic restoring forces (Duffing oscillator) or nonlinear damping (van der Pol oscillator).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 (velocity-cubed damping)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (aerodynamic drag-like damping, approximated as c1*v**2 with sign)
- Forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Forced harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven damped oscillator)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (quadratic + cubic nonlinearity with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear restoring force → term proportional to -x (simple harmonic motion, always present as dominant term)
- Cubic position dependence → x**3 term indicates Duffing-type hardening or softening spring nonlinearity
- Velocity-position coupling → v*x**2 or v*x terms indicate van der Pol-type nonlinear damping or self-excitation
- Odd-power restoring forces → x, x**3, x**5 preserve symmetry of the potential well (symmetric oscillators)
- Even-power restoring forces → x**2 terms break symmetry, indicating asymmetric potential wells
- Periodic explicit time dependence → sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic forcing/driving
- Negative linear damping with positive cubic velocity → c0*v + c1*v**3 indicates limit cycle behavior (Rayleigh oscillator)
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system, phase-plane analysis applicable, formula depends only on x and v

- `-0.721004*v + 0.721004*v**3 - 1.03737*v - 2.44077*x*0.015413*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 2.44077*x`
- `= -2.44077*x - 1.75837*v + 0.721004*v**3 - 0.037617*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`

So GT = **-2.44077*x - 1.75837*v + 0.721004*v**3 - 0.037617*x*Abs(v)^(1/3)**

The key basis functions are:
1. `x` (linear in x)
2. `v` (linear in v)
3. `v**3` (cubic in v)

The term `x * Abs(v)**(1/3)` is critical and unusual. Let me check each candidate for this term.

Most candidates lack the `x * Abs(v)**(1/3)` term. Let me quickly scan for candidates that could potentially produce this term:

- No candidate explicitly contains `Abs(v)**(1/3)` or `|v|^(1/3)`.
- The GT has 4 linearly independent basis functions: `x`, `v`, `v³`, and `x·|v|^(1/3)`.

Let me check candidates that might approximate or match:

**Candidates with `v**3` terms:** 17, 30, 31, 33, 34, 99, 116, etc. But none of these have `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`.

None of the candidates contain the essential `x * Abs(v)**(1/3)` term. Since `Abs(v)**(1/3)` cannot be expressed as any combination of the basis functions present in the candidates (polynomials, exponentials, trigonometric, logarithmic functions of v), and by the principle of linear independence of basis functions, no candidate can match.
